  labels, Gaussian zero degree, square-weighted degree formula, full-label
  log-volume compatibility, and target chart comparison are tied to the same
  corridor facts.
\item The finite-divisor vertical-\(IQ\) Hodge/\(\SHE/\IPL\)/hull endpoint now
  has a source-derived form: it consumes this separated bridge object instead
  of a prebuilt route alignment before constructing the same finite-divisor
  Step (x) source and proving the \(C_\Theta=-1\) boundary alternative or
  strict \(C_\Theta>-1\) conclusion.
\item The same finite-divisor vertical-\(IQ\) endpoint now also has the
  milestone-facing constructor form: it consumes the finite Hodge/\(\SHE\)
  transport source, a Theorem 3.11 \(\IPL\)-link construction source,
  record-native Step (xi) hull data, and the theta/Hodge calibration
  certificate directly.  The Step (xi) inputs are the record's possible-image
  union, \(q\subseteq P_{\mathrm{rec}}\), the holomorphic hull shadow, weighted
  determinant source, tensor-power bound, and bridge equality.  The endpoint
  constructs the \(\IPL\) log-volume transport, the hull/determinant source,
  and the source-derived Hodge/\(\SHE/\IPL\)/hull bridge internally, then
  applies the finite-divisor vertical-\(IQ\) route.
\item The constructor-backed finite-divisor endpoint now preserves the
  Remark~3.9.5 product-hull provenance.  A product-hull-backed wrapper records
  that the measured hull operator is induced by the product-hull system, and the
  audit proves selected-product-hull equality, q-pilot containment, minimality
  among product hulls containing \(P_{\mathrm{rec}}\), product-hull log-volume
  equality, and the same raw \(q_{\mathrm{signed}}\leq\theta_{\mathrm{signed}}\)
  comparison before returning the downstream \(C_\Theta\) dichotomy.  The same
  wrapper now also exposes the Ob5 quotient/determinant compatibility at this
  product-hull boundary: for any nonempty comparison possible image, the q-choice
  possible image and comparison possible image have the same collapsed
  upper-semi quotient image modulo the selected product hull, and the selected
  hull log-volume is identified with the normalized determinant, determinant
  log-volume, and normalized tensor-power value.  The Ob5 scalar companion is
  now explicit as well: after quotienting the real line by the singleton
  \(\{\mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B))\}\), the normalized determinant scalar, ordinary
  determinant scalar, normalized tensor-power scalar, and family-hull
  log-volume scalar all have the same collapsed image.  This records the
  Remark~3.9.5(Ob5) assertion that the upper-semi formalism applies compatibly
  to \(\phi(P_B)\), \(\det^{\otimes M}(\phi(P_B))\), and
  \(\mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B))\).  Finally, the product-hull
  wrapper now projects to the source-facing possible-image family package: the
  Theorem~3.11 family \(P_B\), its canonical \(\Phi(P_B)\) approximant, and any
  supplied exact \(\Xi(P_B)\) family are audited at the same boundary, with
  \(H_{\Xi(P_B)}\) identified with the selected product hull.  The Ob6
  hull-approximant log-volume audit is also exposed at this boundary:
  \(H_{\Phi(P_B)}\) and \(H_{\Xi(P_B)}\) are both identified with the selected
  product hull, while the raw family union, comparison possible image, and
  q-pilot region are estimated by the corresponding hull-approximant
  log-volumes before the normalized determinant equality is invoked.  The same
  boundary now carries an exact-theta bridge audit: the package value
  \(\theta_{\mathrm{signed}}\) is identified with the Remark~3.9.5 family-hull
  log-volume, the normalized tensor-power/determinant upper bound is derived
  from this equality, and the q-pilot log-volume comparison is threaded through
  the selected product hull into \(\theta_{\mathrm{signed}}\).
\item The milestone-facing endpoint has a Hodge--Arakelov source form as well:
  it consumes source and target Hodge--Arakelov theta-evaluation sources,
  canonical one-label degree preservation, and a typed allowed-forgetting
  witness, then constructs the finite Hodge/\(\SHE\) transport internally.  In
  this form the canonical square-weight profile and theta-root source are read
  directly from the Hodge--Arakelov source side before the endpoint applies the
  same Theorem 3.11 \(\IPL\), record-native Step (xi), and finite-divisor
  vertical-\(IQ\) route.
\item A stronger Hodge--Arakelov endpoint removes even that explicit
  allowed-forgetting argument: it builds the finite Hodge/\(\SHE\) transport
  with the record's history-separated descent-bridge permission, then follows
  the same \(\IPL\), record-native Step (xi), and finite-divisor
  vertical-\(IQ\) path.
\item The strongest Hodge--Arakelov/history-separated endpoint can now use the
  certificate-pinned \(\IPL\)-link source.  Its public assumptions no longer
  include an arbitrary finite Hodge/\(\SHE\) transport, a free
  allowed-forgetting predicate, a free square-weight profile, a separate
  theta-root source, a constructed-\(\IPL\)-datum alignment, or the raw
  record-native Step (xi) hull/determinant field list.
\item The target-side theta-to-entry equality is no longer a direct input in the
  strongest route.  It is derived from a Step (x) theta-target alignment and
  calibration of the entry target with the upper-semi target value.
\item The Step (x) theta-target alignment can itself be derived from
  packet-normalized theta-source equality and calibration of the upper-semi
  target with the packet-normalized value.
\item The entry-target calibration can likewise be expressed by equality to the
  packet-normalized value, deriving equality with the upper-semi target.
\item The Step (xi-f) real algebra proves \(C_\Theta\ge-1\), strictness under
  strict upper-ray membership, and equality constraints in the boundary case.
\item The final route rejects the balanced sign-compatible comparison level as
  sufficient; it requires hull/log-volume comparison data.
\item The local Frobenioid shift model is now sourced by a \(p_v^N\)
  log-volume action package and a global realified calibration package; a
  non-automorphic local shift with nonzero step is separated from the calibrated
  value, and the upper-ray quotient experiment gives the exact threshold for
  collapse versus separation in the boundary upper ray.
\item Several downstream \IUT{} IV numerical estimates are formalized as
  ordered-real algebra conditional on the Corollary 3.12 input.
\end{enumerate}

The first-pass experiment report evaluates the route-theorem, finite Gaussian,
collapse-obstruction, upper-ray, and \IUT{} IV algebra flags to
\texttt{true}.  The flag \texttt{disputeSettledByCurrentStage} remains
\texttt{false}.

The current code base is large enough to distinguish three meanings of
``available''.  First, pure ordered-real consequences are proved outright.
Second, route theorems prove that certain named source-facing records imply the
desired endpoint.  Third, the records themselves remain obligations when they
stand for Hodge-theater, Frobenioid, log-Kummer, hull, determinant, or
multiradial constructions not yet formalized from \IUT{} I--III.  Only the first
two meanings are currently achieved.

\section{What Is Not Yet Proved}

No formal statement currently proves \IUT{} III, Corollary 3.12 from
Mochizuki's published hypotheses.  The following mathematics is still external
to the code:

\begin{enumerate}
\item initial \(\Theta\)-data and its arithmetic hypotheses from \IUT{} I;
\item Hodge theaters, Frobenioids, log-shells, prime strips, and theta links;
\item the Hodge--Arakelov theta evaluation and Gaussian monoids of \IUT{} II;
\item the construction of the actual \((\Ind1),(\Ind2),(\Ind3)\) data in
  Theorem 3.11;
\item the genuine holomorphic hull and determinant constructions used in
  Step (xi), beyond the present source-data constructor and ordered-real
  upper-ray model;
\item the full proof that the typed \SHE{} and Hodge-descent transport
  obligations follow from Mochizuki's source constructions, beyond the current
  Hodge--Arakelov canonical-one synchronization shadow;
\item the construction of the input prime-strip link \((\IPL)\), simultaneous
  holomorphic expressibility \((\SHE)\), and algorithmic parallel transport
  \((\APT)\) properties as actual consequences of Theorem 3.11 rather than
  records;
\item the arithmetic-divisor, height, log-different, and log-conductor
  constructions behind the \IUT{} IV Diophantine applications.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Implementation Audit}

The code contains no explicit placeholder proofs or project-level trust-boundary declarations in the
Stage 1 corridor.  The current risk is not hidden unsoundness of this form, but
mathematical incompleteness: several records are deliberately named
obligation interfaces.  These interfaces are acceptable only as temporary
boundaries.  The next phase must replace them by constructions from the source
papers or mark them as unresolved.

For the Source-Derived Step (xi) Bridge milestone, the checked public endpoint is
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{Iut.Stage1.Experiments.boundarySignedEqualityOrStrictCTheta\_from}\\
\quad\texttt{\_sourceDerivedHodgeSHEIPLHullFiniteDivisorVerticalIQ}.
\end{array}
\]
Its direct audit companion is
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{Iut.Stage1.Experiments.boundarySignedEqualityOrStrictCTheta\_from}\\
\quad\texttt{\_sourceDerivedHodgeSHEIPLHullFiniteDivisorVerticalIQ}\\
\quad\texttt{\_withDirectMilestoneAudit}.
\end{array}
\]
Both declarations have been added to the \texttt{checkdecls} list.  A kernel
\texttt{\#print axioms} check for these two declarations, the explicit
constructed-\(\IPL\) alias, and the underlying namespaced constructed-\(\IPL\)
endpoint reports only \texttt{propext}, \texttt{Classical.choice}, and
\texttt{Quot.sound}; in particular, no \texttt{sorryAx} appears.  Thus the
milestone is kernel-clean at the usual Lean classical/quotient trust boundary.

The Remark~3.9.5 holomorphic-hull/determinant milestone has now started at the
source-object level.  The new declaration
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395HolomorphicHullOperator} records the source-facing
\(\phi\)-operator laws directly: closed hulls are fixed, \(P\subseteq\phi(P)\),
inclusions are preserved, \(\phi(\phi(P))=\phi(P)\), and log-volume is
monotone.  It projects to the older closure-operator shadow used by the
existing bridge code, but the public source object no longer begins with that
shadow.  This has now been backed by the earlier construction in
Remark~3.9.5(ii): \texttt{IUTStage1Remark395HolomorphicHullSystem} defines
\(\phi(P)\) as the intersection of all hulls that contain \(P\).  Its only
source closure input is that this intersection is again a hull; \Lean{} then
derives P1--P3, idempotence, and
\(\mu_{\log}(P)\leq\mu_{\log}(\phi(P))\), before projecting to the existing
\(\phi\)-operator interface.
The possible-image family layer has also been made source-facing:
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395PossibleImageFamilySource} records the family
\(P_B=\{P_\beta\}_{\beta\in B}\), its union, the canonical hull
\(\phi(P_B)\), the \(\Phi(P_B)\) and \(\Xi(P_B)\) approximant types projected
from this \(\phi\)-operator, and the Remark~3.9.5(Ob5) upper-semi quotient
collapse.  The experiment-surface declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{Iut.Stage1.Experiments.remark395PossibleImageFamilySource\_endpoint}
\end{array}
\]
proves that the family union and each possible image lie in \(\phi(P_B)\), that
the canonical \(\Phi\)-approximant is \(\phi(P_B)\), and that any two nonempty
possible regions have the same quotient image after collapsing \(\phi(P_B)\).
The exact-approximant companion
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{Iut.Stage1.Experiments.remark395PossibleImageFamilySource}\\
\quad\texttt{\_XiFamilyOb5Endpoint}
\end{array}
\]
proves the same Ob5 collapse for \(H_{\Xi(P_B)}\), while recording that each
chosen exact approximant has log-volume \(\mu_{\log}(P_B)\).
This supplied-family endpoint is now accompanied by the more source-local
constructor
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{Iut.Stage1.Experiments.remark395PossibleImageExactXiFamilySource}\\
\quad\texttt{\_toXiFamilyOb5Endpoint}
\end{array}
\]
and its Ob6 companion.  These endpoints start only from the exactness
calibration \(\mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B))=\mu_{\log}(P_B)\), build the canonical
exact \(\Xi(P_B)\)-family, and then recover the same quotient collapse and
log-volume comparison.  Thus this part of the corridor now records the
specific mathematical equality needed to make \(\phi(P_B)\) exact, instead of
treating the whole \(\Xi(P_B)\)-family as primitive.
The same boundary has now been lowered to the concrete Hodge-theater/log-theta
quotient source.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{concreteHodgeTheaterLogThetaConcreteCalibratedExactXi}\\
\quad\texttt{SelectedQRemark395GlobalCThetaAudit}
\end{array}
\]
constructs the exact \(\Xi(P_B)\)-source from the typed quotient
possible-image family and a single source-local calibration
\(\mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B))=\mu_{\log}(P_B)\).  Hence the remaining analytic
payload is no longer a primitive exact-\(\Xi\) family; it is precisely the
paper-side proof of this calibration for the selected quotient possible-image
union.
For the closed-family case this has been lowered once more.  The source
\texttt{ConcreteClosedFamilyUnionExactXiSource} asks only that the concrete
quotient possible-image union be closed for the Remark~3.9.5 hull operator;
\Lean{} then proves \(\phi(P_B)=P_B\) by the hull fixing law and derives
\(\mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B))=\mu_{\log}(P_B)\).  Thus the exactness obligation is
now split into a closed-region route and the remaining non-closed analytic
calibration route.
The closed-region route now has product-hull provenance.  The source
\texttt{ConcreteProductHullFamilyUnionExactXiSource} replaces bare closedness
by the assertion that the quotient possible-image union is a product hull for
the Remark~3.9.5 product-hull system whose induced holomorphic hull operator is
the corridor operator.  From this product-hull witness, \Lean{} constructs the
closed-family exact-\(\Xi(P_B)\) source and enters the same global
\(C_\Theta\) audit.  This has a principal valuation-ball refinement:
\texttt{ConcretePrincipalValuationBallFamilyUnionExactXiSource} starts from a
Remark~3.9.5 valuation-ball product-hull cover and identifies the resulting
valuation-cover union with the selected principal hull \(\lambda\cdot O\).
The sharper source
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallIndexedFamilyUnionSource} no longer takes the
quotient-family/valuation-cover union equality as primitive: it requires an
equivalence between the Theorem~3.11 quotient index and the valuation-cover
index, plus pointwise equality of the corresponding possible regions, and
\Lean{} derives the union equality.  This comparison has now been lowered one
more step by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallChoiceIndexedFamilyUnionSource}: instead of
supplying the quotient-index equivalence, the source data supplies a
choice-level valuation index map, proves that it is invariant under the
typed \((\Ind1,\Ind2)\) equality quotient, gives a representative
Hodge-theater/log-theta choice over each valuation index, and proves pointwise
equality of the corresponding possible regions.  \Lean{} constructs the
quotient-index equivalence by \texttt{Quot.lift} and then derives the same
valuation-cover union equality.  The current preferred form specializes this
once more to the theta-pilot class itself:
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassIndexedFamilyUnionSource} fixes the
valuation-cover index to the forgotten Hodge-theater/log-theta-lattice class,
proves theta-class invariance across the generated \((\Ind1,\Ind2)\) equality
relation, and derives the choice-indexed valuation source from representative
choices in each theta class.  This has now been lowered to the fiber-backed
source
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberBackedFamilyUnionSource}.  Its
representative fiber relation is no longer supplied: \Lean{} builds the
representative-to-choice relation as the canonical finite \((\Ind1)\)
procession shift followed by the typed post-procession \((\Ind2)\) local
tensor transport already present in the Theorem~3.11 source audit.  The
valuation-indexing payload at this boundary is therefore only the pointwise
equality between quotient possible regions and theta-class valuation cells.
That pointwise quotient comparison has now also been factored through concrete
theta-pilot possible images.  The source
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassImageBackedFamilyUnionSource} supplies a
theta-pilot-class possible-image family, identifies the record's
choice-indexed possible images with the pullback of that class family, and
identifies each class image with the corresponding valuation-ball region.
\Lean{} then uses the Theorem~3.11 equality-quotient pullback theorem to derive
the quotient-region/valuation-region comparison required by the older
fiber-backed boundary.  This has now been lowered through
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassRegionBackedFamilyUnionSource} and
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassLatticeFormulaBackedFamilyUnionSource}.
At this new boundary, the possible images are generated by the
Hodge-theater id, history label, finite-label-forgotten log-theta-lattice
coordinate, and coric datum already present in the concrete
Hodge-theater/log-theta-lattice formula records.  The valuation comparison is
then a source-facing identification between those lattice-formula theta regions
and the corresponding valuation-ball regions, not an arbitrary
choice-indexed quotient comparison.  The boundary has now been lowered one
step further by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassLatticeImageLawBackedFamilyUnionSource}.
Here \Lean{} constructs the lattice formula and the record-level family
equality from a single lattice-key invariance law: choices with the same
Hodge-theater id, history label, finite-label-forgotten log-theta-lattice
coordinate, and coric datum have the same Theorem~3.11 possible-image region.
The boundary has now been lowered again by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportBackedFamilyUnionSource}.
The lattice-key image law is no longer the primitive source input: the current
packet/action transport source is first forgotten through the typed
\((\Ind1,\Ind2)\) procession/local-tensor chain to a theta-pilot
fiber-transport invariant possible-image family, and \Lean{} derives the
lattice image law from that fiber-transport invariance.  The valuation-side
payload at this point is therefore the identification of the derived
theta-pilot class regions with the corresponding valuation-ball regions.
The log-volume side of this same concrete choice space has now been lowered by
\texttt{ProcessionNormalizedLogVolumeSource}.  Instead of accepting an
arbitrary \texttt{IndeterminacyData} record, the source assigns to each
theta-pilot class an actual averaged \(Z/\ell Z\)-label procession log-volume.
\Lean{} defines the log-volume of a concrete Hodge-theater/log-theta choice as
this class average, proves the displayed average formula with
\(|Z/\ell Z|=\ell\), derives the old \texttt{IndeterminacyData} record, and
constructs the typed core used by the quotient possible-image machinery.  Thus
the equality side of the indeterminacy layer is now built from finite
procession averages; only the \((\Ind3)\) upper-semi comparison remains a
one-sided source input at this boundary.  The next lowering is now also in
place: \texttt{LogThetaLabelProcessionUpperSemiSource} supplies the
label-by-label log-theta values over the canonical full \(F_\ell\)-procession
of a theta-pilot class, and \Lean{} constructs the averaged source internally.
The open mathematical input below this point is the source-paper construction
of those label-wise values and the two average equalities with the
source/target upper-semi log-volume comparison.
The selected-principal-hull equality has also been lowered:
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallSelectedPrincipalHullSource}
requires the valuation-cover possible-image union to be a hull for its
Remark~3.9.5 hull system, and \Lean{} combines this fixed-point statement with
the principal-hull selection theorem to derive equality with the selected
\(\lambda\cdot O\) hull.  This has now been lowered to the direct-product-cell
exact source
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallDirectProductCellUnionExactSource}: it records
that the valuation possible-image union is exactly the finite union of the
valuation-ball direct-product cells, and \Lean{} derives both hull-fixedness
and equality with the selected principal hull from the already formalized
Remark~3.9.5 principal-hull theorem.  The preferred boundary has now been
lowered once more by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallDirectProductCellCoverSource}.  Here the formal
direction
\[
  \bigcup P_{\Theta} \subseteq \bigcup_{\beta} H_{\beta}
\]
comes from hull containment together with the valuation-cover theorem
\(\phi(\bigcup P_{\Theta})=\bigcup_{\beta}H_{\beta}\).  The only source-facing
payload is the reverse local cover statement: every valuation-ball
direct-product cell \(H_{\beta}\) lies in the theta possible-image union.
This has now been sharpened by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassDirectProductCellCoverSource}: each
valuation cell carries a theta-pilot class, and the local cover proof is the
containment of that cell in the corresponding theta-class possible region.
\Lean{} derives the older union-cover interface from these per-cell
containments.  The transported-region version
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportCellCoverSource} states
the containment before forgetting to the valuation cover, i.e. each
\(H_\beta\) lies in the transported theta-class region attached to its
theta-pilot class, and \Lean{} derives both the valuation-region equality
interface and the theta-class cell cover.  The current preferred boundary is
one step lower:
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportLocalFactorCoverSource}.
For each valuation cell it chooses a theta-pilot class and a local place, and
requires containment of the corresponding compact-open valuation-ball factor in
the transported theta-class region.  Since \(H_\beta\) is the direct product of
these local factors, \Lean{} derives the previous whole-cell containment.  The
preferred boundary is now the local predicate source
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportLocalThetaPredicateSource}.
For the selected local place it identifies the transported theta region with
the realization of a local predicate \(T_\beta(x)\), and requires the local
estimate
\[
  \|x\|_v\le r_\beta
  \quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  T_\beta(x),
\]
where \(r_\beta\) is the compact-open radius chosen by the local Haar
normalization.  \Lean{} realizes this predicate region to recover the pointwise
theta membership, then uses
\(\mathrm{realizedRegion}(S)=\mathrm{realization}(S)\) and the valuation-ball
audit \(\mathrm{compactOpenSubset}=\mathrm{valuationBall}(r_\beta)\) to recover
the valuation-radius, local-factor, and direct-product cell covers.  This has
now been lowered one step further by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportLocalThetaInequalitySource}.
Here the local predicate is not opaque: it is the inequality
\[
  g_\beta(x)\le R_\beta
\]
for a named local theta gauge and threshold, and the source estimate proves
\[
  \|x\|_v\le r_\beta\quad\Longrightarrow\quad g_\beta(x)\le R_\beta.
\]
\Lean{} then reconstructs the local-predicate source definitionally and enters
the same exact-\(\Xi(P_B)\) and global \(C_\Theta\) corridor.  The gauge has now
been specialized to the valuation-ball normalization itself by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationNormGaugeSource}:
\[
  g_\beta(x)=\|x\|_v,\qquad R_\beta=r_\beta .
\]
Thus the implication
\(\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\Rightarrow g_\beta(x)\le R_\beta\) is no longer a
mathematical assumption.  The equality boundary has also been lowered twice.
First,
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallExactSource}
replaces the two equalities needed by the valuation-norm gauge source with the
two inclusions
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}\subseteq \mathrm{realizedRegion}(B_\beta),
  \qquad
  \mathrm{realizedRegion}(B_\beta)\subseteq P_{\Theta,\beta}
\]
and the analogous two inclusions between a transported theta-class region and
the valuation-cover possible-image region.  \Lean{} reconstructs both
equalities by antisymmetry and then enters the same valuation-norm-gauge
endpoint.  The next boundary is the pointwise source
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallPointwiseSource}.
It replaces the set containments by the local lifting law
\[
  y\in P_{\Theta,\beta}\Longrightarrow
  \exists x,\ \|x\|_v\le r_\beta\ \wedge\ \mathrm{realization}(x)=y,
\]
the reverse realization law
\[
  \|x\|_v\le r_\beta\Longrightarrow
  \mathrm{realization}(x)\in P_{\Theta,\beta},
\]
and pointwise membership compatibility with the valuation-cover possible
regions.  The set containments and equalities are now projections from these
local transport laws.  This lifting law has now been lowered once more by
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallLocalChartSource}:
for each transported theta point \(y\), the source names its local coordinate
\(x_\beta(y)\), proves
\[
  \|x_\beta(y)\|_v\le r_\beta,\qquad
  \mathrm{realization}(x_\beta(y))=y.
\]
This removes the existential lift, but at this stage the valuation-radius bound
is still a raw source field.
The image boundary is now an intermediate layer:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallLogShellImageSource}.
\end{array}
\]
It names a local log-shell region \(I_\beta\), a base point used only outside
the transported theta region, the realized-image equality presented as the two
containments
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}\subseteq \mathrm{realization}(I_\beta),
  \qquad
  \mathrm{realization}(I_\beta)\subseteq P_{\Theta,\beta},
\]
and the two valuation-ball containments
\[
  I_\beta\subseteq \{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\},
  \qquad
  \{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\subseteq I_\beta.
\]
\Lean{} chooses \(x_\beta(y)\) from the image statement when
\(y\in P_{\Theta,\beta}\), proves \(x_\beta(y)\in I_\beta\) and
\(\mathrm{realization}(x_\beta(y))=y\), derives the valuation-radius inequality
from \(I_\beta\subseteq \{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\), and then reuses the
local-chart, pointwise, exact, and valuation-norm-gauge routes.
The next boundary replaces these four containments by the two equalities
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallLogShellExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
It requires
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}=\mathrm{realization}(I_\beta),
  \qquad
  I_\beta=\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\},
\]
and \Lean{} derives the previous log-shell image source, the chosen local
coordinate, the valuation-radius bound, and the same exact-\(\Xi(P_B)\)/global
\(C_\Theta\) audit.  The next boundary is
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallLogShellNonemptyExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
It replaces the supplied totalizing coordinate by the nonemptiness statement
\(I_\beta\ne\varnothing\); \Lean{} chooses the auxiliary coordinate from this
nonemptiness and then projects to the equality-backed exact source.  The
preferred lower boundary is now
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportValuationBallNonemptyExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
It moves nonemptiness to the valuation-ball side:
\[
  \{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\ne\varnothing.
\]
Using \(I_\beta=\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\), \Lean{} derives
\(I_\beta\ne\varnothing\), then derives the previous nonempty log-shell
boundary and the same exact-\(\Xi(P_B)\)/global \(C_\Theta\) audit.  This
nonemptiness hypothesis has now itself been lowered to a centered valuation
ball source:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportCenteredValuationBall}\\
\texttt{ExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
For each local factor it supplies a point \(x_\beta\) and proves
\[
  \|x_\beta\|_v \le r_\beta.
\]
After unfolding the valuation-ball definition, \Lean{} obtains
\(x_\beta\in\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\), hence valuation-ball nonemptiness,
log-shell nonemptiness, and the same exact-\(\Xi(P_B)\)/global \(C_\Theta\)
audit.  This has now been lowered once more to the zero-centered source
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportZeroCenteredValuationBall}\\
\texttt{ExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
Here the center is fixed to \(0\).  The source supplies only
\[
  \|0\|_v \le r_\beta,
\]
and \Lean{} constructs the centered source with \(x_\beta=0\).  The next
boundary is metric-normalized:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportMetricZeroValuationBall}\\
\texttt{ExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
It no longer supplies the zero inequality.  Instead it records, for each
local factor, the normalization
\[
  \|x\|_v=\operatorname{dist}(x,0).
\]
Together with the already available positivity \(0<r_\beta\), \Lean{} proves
\(\|0\|_v\le r_\beta\) using \(\operatorname{dist}(0,0)=0\), then projects to
the zero-centered endpoint.  The log-shell boundary has also been lowered:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportConstructedLogShell}\\
\texttt{MetricZeroValuationBallExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
Here the local log-shell attached to a factor is no longer an independent
set.  It is defined to be the compact-open valuation ball
\[
  \{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\},
\]
so the log-shell/valuation-ball equality is definitional.  The remaining
realization equality has now been factored into pointwise local transport:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportPointwiseConstructed}\\
\texttt{LogShellMetricZeroValuationBallExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
This source no longer supplies
\(\Theta_\beta=\operatorname{realize}(\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\})\) directly.
It supplies the two local assertions: every transported theta-region point has
a lift in the compact-open valuation ball, and every local point in that ball
realizes back into the transported theta region.  \Lean{} converts these
assertions to the two set inclusions using the factor's
\(\texttt{realizedRegion\_eq\_image}\) law and then obtains the equality by
antisymmetry.  A further source,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportRegionBackedPointwise}\\
\texttt{ConstructedLogShellMetricZeroValuationBallExactSource},
\end{array}
\]
removes the duplicated pointwise membership assumptions at this boundary.  It
uses the fiber-transport-backed equality
\[
  \Theta_{\mathrm{class}}=
  P_{\Theta_{\mathrm{class}}}
\]
between the transported theta-class region and the valuation-cover possible
region, and \Lean{} derives the two membership directions by rewriting.  The
classwise equality is now itself derived from the sharper source
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{FamilyUnionSource}.
\end{array}
\]
There the valuation-cover possible-region family is identified once with the
transported theta-region family; evaluating this family equality at a
theta-pilot class gives the previous classwise comparison.  The corresponding
pointwise source then reuses this family-level construction when deriving
valuation-cover membership.  The construction boundary has now moved inside
the valuation cover:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{ValuationCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
builds the Remark~3.9.5 valuation-ball/Haar tensor-packet cover with
\(P_\beta\) fixed definitionally to the transported theta-region family.  Its
principal product-hull wrapper projects to the ordinary principal
valuation-ball source, and the previous family-level equality is then
\texttt{rfl}.  This boundary now also has a source-core constructor: a
Remark~3.9.5 factor-calibrated valuation-ball/Haar cover, or its principal
valuation-ball product-hull wrapper, constructs the theta-region-defined
Step~(xi) cover as soon as its possible-image family is identified with the
transported theta-region family.  The newest constructor derives this
family-level equality from the fiber-transport-backed pointwise comparison by
function extensionality, and there is now a lattice-image-law-backed version:
once the lattice image law used in the valuation comparison is identified with
the one produced by the fiber-transport source, the same principal
theta-region-defined cover is constructed.  When the lattice law is obtained
by projecting a fiber-transport-backed source, this identification is now a
named \texttt{rfl} theorem and the public endpoint routes through the
lattice-image-law constructor without an extra equality argument.  Thus the
finite-additive Haar tensor factors, principal \(\lambda O\) hull,
local-integer region, and selected-hull log-volume identity are inherited from
the source-core object instead of being re-supplied in the Step~(xi) source.
The remaining source-facing payload at this boundary is the construction of
the fiber-transport comparison itself, and for independently supplied lattice
laws the proof that they are the fiber-transport lattice law, from the
paper-native log-theta transport.  The local analytic boundary is now
connected directly to this constructed principal cover:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{PrincipalValuationBallPointwiseConstructedLogShellMetricZero}\\
\texttt{ValuationBallExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
This source carries the metric normalization \(\|x\|_v=\operatorname{dist}(x,0)\)
and the two pointwise local transport laws between transported theta-region
points and compact-open valuation balls, while the valuation-cover
possible-region family is fixed definitionally by the principal source.  \Lean{}
derives the realized valuation-ball equality, projects it to the
theta-region-defined radius-cover source, obtains direct-product-cell exactness,
and then feeds the principal exact-\(\Xi\) source.  Thus the remaining
paper-side payload has been narrowed to the actual construction of the local
analytic coordinate and the reverse valuation-ball realization law.  The newest
declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{PrincipalValuationBallLocalChartMetricZeroValuationBallExactSource}
\end{array}
\]
replaces the forward existential lifting law by a named map
\(x_\beta(y)\in K_v\).  Its fields assert the valuation-radius bound
\(\|x_\beta(y)\|_v\le r_\beta\), the realization identity
\(\operatorname{real}_\beta(x_\beta(y))=y\), the metric normalization, and the
reverse statement that each selected valuation-ball point realizes back into
the transported theta region.  \Lean{} derives the pointwise lift, recovers the
previous principal pointwise source, and hence recovers the exact realized
valuation-ball identity and selected-principal-hull conclusion.  This boundary
has now been lowered to an image-backed log-shell source:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{PrincipalValuationBallLogShellImageMetricZeroValuationBallExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
Instead of supplying \(x_\beta(y)\) as chart data, it records the two
containments
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}\subseteq \operatorname{real}_\beta(I_\beta),
  \qquad
  \operatorname{real}_\beta(I_\beta)\subseteq P_{\Theta,\beta},
\]
and the two containments identifying \(I_\beta\) with the compact-open
valuation ball.  \Lean{} chooses \(x_\beta(y)\) from the first image
containment, proves \(\operatorname{real}_\beta(x_\beta(y))=y\), derives the
radius bound from \(I_\beta\subseteq\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\), and derives the
reverse realization law from
\(\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\subseteq I_\beta\) together with the second image
containment.  The log-shell itself has now been lowered to the compact-open
local shell:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{PrincipalValuationBallCompactOpenLogShellImageMetricZero}\\
\texttt{ValuationBallExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
Here \(I_\beta\) is definitionally the selected factor's compact-open subset.
The equality between this compact-open subset and
\(\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\) is read from the valuation-ball additive Haar
normalization audit, so the two log-shell/valuation-ball containments are no
longer source fields.  The preferred boundary has also been lowered once more
to a compact-open local-chart source:
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{PrincipalValuationBallCompactOpenLocalChartMetricZero}\\
\texttt{ValuationBallExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
This source gives compact-open representatives
\(x_\beta(y)\in U_\beta\) for transported theta-region points and the converse
law that every \(u\in U_\beta\) realizes back into \(P_{\Theta,\beta}\).
Using the valuation-ball additive Haar identity
\(U_\beta=\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\}\), it now also constructs the pointwise
valuation-ball source that feeds log-shell exactness.
Using the local analytic identity
\(\operatorname{realizedRegion}(U_\beta)=\operatorname{real}_\beta''U_\beta\),
\Lean{} derives the two compact-open image containments
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}\subseteq
    \operatorname{real}_\beta(U_\beta),
  \qquad
  \operatorname{real}_\beta(U_\beta)\subseteq P_{\Theta,\beta}
\]
and then enters the source-derived global \(C_\Theta\) audit.  The remaining
frontier has now been lowered to the exact compact-open realized-region source
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{ConcreteValuationBallThetaClassFiberTransportThetaRegionDefined}\\
\texttt{PrincipalValuationBallCompactOpenRealizedExactSource}.
\end{array}
\]
Its local payload is the single identity
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}=\operatorname{real}_\beta(U_\beta).
\]
From this equality and
\(\operatorname{realizedRegion}(U_\beta)=\operatorname{real}_\beta''U_\beta\),
\Lean{} chooses compact-open coordinates, proves the converse realization law,
recovers the compact-open local-chart source, and enters the same global
\(C_\Theta\) audit.  This compact-open boundary is now itself a projection from
the valuation-ball realized-exact source: if
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}
    =\operatorname{realizedRegion}\{x:\|x\|_v\le r_\beta\},
\]
then the valuation-ball additive Haar audit identifies the selected
compact-open subset \(U_\beta\) with this closed ball, and \Lean{} derives the
compact-open realized source.  The equality-backed log-shell package is also
now recovered from local containments.  On the compact-open branch, the two
image containments
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}\subseteq \operatorname{realizedRegion}(U_\beta),\quad
  \operatorname{realizedRegion}(U_\beta)\subseteq P_{\Theta,\beta}
\]
already construct the compact-open realized-exact source by antisymmetry, so
the preferred \(C_\Theta\) audit no longer has to pass through an arbitrary
log-shell equality package.  The more general log-shell source is still
recovered from the four containments
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}\subseteq \operatorname{realizedRegion}(I_\beta),\quad
  \operatorname{realizedRegion}(I_\beta)\subseteq P_{\Theta,\beta},\quad
  I_\beta\subseteq B_\beta(r_\beta),\quad
  B_\beta(r_\beta)\subseteq I_\beta,
\]
so the source need not assert these set equalities at the first boundary.
The compact-open local-chart boundary has also been lowered through a
log-Kummer graph formulation.  First, a graph source may supply a local
realization relation on \(U_\beta\times P_{\Theta,\beta}\); left-totality,
realization compatibility, and right-soundness recover compact-open
coordinates.  Second, and more canonically, the compact-open image source now
defines this relation to be the graph of the selected realization map
\[
  x\sim_\beta y \quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
  \operatorname{real}_\beta(x)=y .
\]
The two image containments then prove the graph laws.  Thus the local
log-Kummer graph is no longer an independent payload at this boundary.  The
graph source also constructs the pointwise local valuation-ball source:
compact-open graph lifts are converted to valuation-radius lifts by the
additive Haar normalization, and right-soundness gives the converse
valuation-ball realization law.  Thus the graph route can now pass through
pointwise local construction, log-shell exactness, compact-open image
compatibility, and finally the global \(C_\Theta\) audit.
The containments themselves were first lowered to the valuation-cover side by the
single equality
\[
  P_{\mathrm{cover}}(\Theta_\beta)
    =\operatorname{realizedRegion}(U_\beta),
\]
where \(P_{\mathrm{cover}}\) is the Remark~3.9.5 valuation-cover possible
region.  Since the principal cover is constructed with
\(P_{\mathrm{cover}}(\Theta)=P_\Theta\), \Lean{} rewrites this equality to
derive both compact-open image containments, the realized-exact source, and the
canonical graph route.  This equality is now itself derived from a local
log-Kummer image source: every point of
\(P_{\mathrm{cover}}(\Theta_\beta)\) has a lift in \(U_\beta\), and every
point of \(U_\beta\) realizes back into
\(P_{\mathrm{cover}}(\Theta_\beta)\).  That image source now constructs the
map-level local log-Kummer source.  \Lean{} takes the local Kummer realization
map to be the selected valuation-factor realization
\[
  \kappa_\beta:K_\beta\longrightarrow\operatorname{Pt}(\mathbb L_\Theta),
\]
and chooses a section of \(\kappa_\beta\) over the selected
Remark~3.9.5 possible region from canonical graph left-totality.  It then
defines the local correspondence as the graph of \(\kappa_\beta\), derives
realization compatibility, compact-open soundness, the image source, cover
exactness, and the global \(C_\Theta\) audit.  Since the principal cover has
\(P_{\mathrm{cover}}(\Theta_\beta)=P_{\Theta,\beta}\) definitionally, the same
map source now also lowers to the theta-region graph source and hence through
the pointwise valuation-ball, log-shell exact, compact-open image route before
the global \(C_\Theta\) audit.  The compact-open image laws are
now also downstream of a log-shell exact source: the two equalities
\[
  P_{\Theta,\beta}=\operatorname{real}_\beta(L_\beta),
  \qquad L_\beta=U_\beta
\]
construct the compact-open route using the valuation-ball Haar normalization.
These equalities are no longer only accepted as an exact source: the pointwise
local construction, which supplies a local representative of each theta-region
point and the converse realization law for the compact-open valuation ball,
constructs the exact source.  Those pointwise laws are now themselves
constructed from compact-open local-chart data, and the compact-open
log-Kummer graph source projects to that local-chart boundary.  The remaining
frontier is the construction of the graph/local-chart laws from the
paper-native holomorphic hull, log-Kummer, and local log-shell geometry.
There is now also an \texttt{ofHullSystem} constructor and experiment endpoint:
starting from the intersection-defined hull system and a family
\(\{P_\beta\}\), \Lean{} constructs the possible-image source and proves that
the canonical hull is precisely the system's \(\phi(\bigcup_\beta P_\beta)\),
which is a hull by the intersection-closure input.  Thus the Ob5 quotient
collapse for possible images is already downstream of the minimal-hull
construction, not merely of a supplied \(\phi\)-operator.
The product-hull source now has a direct-product constructor as well:
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395DirectProductHullSystemSource} defines product hulls
as coordinate products, defines the selected hull parameter by coordinate
projections of the region, and proves the ``smallest product hull'' equality
before projecting to the existing product-hull and holomorphic-hull systems.
The determinant side now has a source-facing Ob3/Ob4 package as well:

checks the adjusted-summand formula, determinant summation, tensor-power

\texttt{ofOb3Ob4AdjustedDeterminantSource} whose endpoint verifies that this
source-facing Ob3/Ob4 package is the determinant source used by the existing
hull/determinant corridor.
This determinant package now has a lower source-facing constructor layer.  The

separate the local-ring-labelled vector-bundle localization of Step~(xi-d) from

The Ob3/Ob5 determinant-compatibility input has also been separated from the

This object states, at the possible-image-family level, that

Lean derives the older

This route no longer takes the Ob4 tensor-power bound as an independent input.

  \mu_{\log}(q)\leq \det_{\mathrm{norm}}\leq

The record-canonical Ob3/Ob5 source now also has a public constructor endpoint

    =

The pairwise-disjointness input has now been pushed one level lower as well.

The owner map itself has now been constructed from a lower family-hull indexed

The indexing source has now been pushed down to a direct-product localization

represents \(H_\beta\) as the finite direct-product cell cut out by all local

\[
  \phi(P_B)=\bigcup_\beta H_\beta
\]
to choose the unique cell containing a hull point, and then constructs the
family-hull indexed source rather than taking the index map as primitive.
The finite-additivity boundary has also been localized to this same

\[

\quad\texttt{LocalizedHullCoverVectorBundleSource}

does not assume a universal finite-additive law for arbitrary region families.
Instead it records the cover-specific Step~(xi) equality
\[
  \mu_{\log}\!\left(\bigcup_\beta H_\beta\right)
    = \sum_\beta \mu_{\log}(H_\beta)
\]
for the direct-product localization cells.  \Lean{} transports this equality
across the identification of \(H_\beta\) with the calibrated localized regions,
derives the calibrated cover source, and proves
\(\mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B))\) equals the sum of the adjusted Ob3/Ob4 localization
summands.
This cover-specific equality has now been derived from a lower finite
local-factor volume source.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395LocalFactorVolume}\\
\quad\texttt{DirectProductLocalizedHullCoverVectorBundleSource}

assigns a log-volume contribution to each local factor of each direct-product

\[
  \mu_{\log}(H_\beta)=\sum_v \mu_{\beta,v},
  \qquad
  \mu_{\log}\!\left(\bigcup_\beta H_\beta\right)
    =\sum_\beta\sum_v \mu_{\beta,v}.
\]
\Lean{} then derives the direct-product cover additivity by finite-sum
congruence and projects to the cover-specific additive source.  Thus the
previous cover-additivity assumption is now reduced to the local-factor
log-volume computation for the localized arithmetic-vector-bundle cells.
The local-factor volumes are now also tied to the Ob3 vector-bundle data.  The
declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395VectorBundleLocalFactor}\\
\quad\texttt{DirectProductLocalizedHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
defines the local factor \(\mu_{\beta,v}\) to be the direct-summand
log-volume of the localized arithmetic vector bundle attached to \(\beta\) at
the place \(v\).  Its source laws compute each \(H_\beta\) from the associated
bundle log-volume and compute the cover from the resulting finite bundle sum.
\Lean{} then derives the previous local-factor source and proves that the
local-factor sum agrees with the weighted adjusted Ob3/Ob4 summand already
used by the determinant package.  Thus the local-factor layer is no longer an
independent real-valued family; it is read from the localized vector-bundle
summands.
The factor regions themselves have now been pushed down one more source layer.
The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395LocalRingChartedVectorBundle}\\
\quad\texttt{DirectProductHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
introduces a local-ring chart for each factor of each direct-product
localization cell.  The chart records the local-ring label and the region that
represents the corresponding local factor.  Its source laws identify the chart
local ring with the local-ring label of the localized arithmetic vector bundle,
identify each chart log-volume with the associated direct-summand log-volume,
compute each \(H_\beta\) as the sum of these chart-factor log-volumes, and
compute the cover as the finite sum of charted cell log-volumes.  \Lean{} then
derives the vector-bundle local-factor source.  Thus the regions entering the
direct-product cover are no longer an arbitrary family parallel to the bundle
data; they are read from local-ring localization charts tied to the same
localized vector bundles.
The chart/bundle matching has also been isolated at the individual factor
level.  The new
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1LocalRingVectorBundleFactorCalibrationSource}
\end{array}
\]
records, for a fixed \((\beta,v)\), that the chart lies over the same local
ring as the localized arithmetic vector bundle and that the chart region's
log-volume is the corresponding direct-summand log-volume.  The aggregate
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395CalibratedLocalRingCharted}\\
\quad\texttt{VectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
then builds the previous charted direct-product source from these per-factor
calibrations, together with the remaining cell factorization and cover
additivity laws.  This separates the local-ring/direct-summand calibration
obligation from the finite direct-product geometry obligation.
The cover additivity law has now been separated from the calibrated charted
source as well.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395FiniteAdditiveCalibrated}\\
\quad\texttt{LocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
keeps the same per-factor calibrations and cell-factorization law, but replaces
the charted cover log-volume equality by a finite-additive hull log-volume
source.  Distinct direct-product cells are proved disjoint from the local-factor
separation condition, and \Lean{} applies finite additivity to derive
\[
  \mu_{\log}\!\left(\bigcup_\beta H_\beta\right)
    =\sum_\beta \mu_{\log}(H_\beta).
\]
Thus the cover equality consumed by the charted vector-bundle route is no
longer an independent field of that route.
The per-cell direct-product equality has now been factored as well.  The new
source declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1DirectProductCellLogVolumeSource}
\end{array}
\]
records the Step~(xi-d) tensor/direct-product log-volume law for one finite
localization cell:
\[
  \mu_{\log}\!\left(\bigcap_v H_{\beta,v}\right)
    =\sum_v \mu_{\log}(H_{\beta,v}).
\]
The aggregate
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395ProductLogVolumeFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
therefore no longer takes the cell-factorization equality as a bare field.  It
derives the equality for each \(H_\beta\) from the single-cell product
log-volume source, proves disjointness from local-factor separation, applies
finite additivity to the direct-product cover, and then projects to the previous
finite-additive charted source.
This source has now been lowered once more to a tensor/direct-sum datum for the
actual charted cells.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1FiniteTensorDirectSumLogVolumeSource}
\end{array}
\]
records a finite tensor-product region, its identification with the corresponding
direct-product cell, the local factor log-volumes, and the finite direct-sum
formula for the tensor-product log-volume.  From these data, \Lean{} derives the
single-cell law
\[
  \mu_{\log}(H_\beta)
    =\sum_v \mu_{\log}(H_{\beta,v}).
\]
The aggregate
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395TensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
assigns such a tensor/direct-sum source to each charted localization cell, derives
the cell log-volume equalities, proves the same pairwise-disjoint cover
additivity, and projects to the finite-additive calibrated charted cover source.
The tensor-cell source has now been lowered to compact-open local factor data.
The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1LocalCompactOpenTensorFactorSource}
\end{array}
\]
records the local ring label, compact-open local factor region, and normalized
local log-volume for one nonarchimedean tensor factor.  A second declaration,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1CompactOpenTensorRegionDirectSumSource}
\end{array}
\]
records the tensor-product region obtained from a finite family of these
compact-open factors, identifies it with the simultaneous local-factor cell, and
proves the finite direct-sum log-volume formula.  Lean then constructs
\(\texttt{IUTStage1FiniteTensorDirectSumLogVolumeSource}\) from this
compact-open direct-sum datum, including the chart-region transport needed when
the compact-open factor regions are identified with the already charted local
factor regions.
At the packet level,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395CompactOpenTensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
requires one such compact-open tensor direct-sum construction for each charted
localization cell, proves that the compact-open factor regions and local-ring
labels match the charted local factors, constructs the tensor-packet source, and
then derives the same finite-additive cover equality and bundle-log-volume
projection.
The compact-open tensor factor source has now been lowered to a
nonarchimedean local normalized log-volume datum.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1NonarchimedeanLocalCompactOpenLogVolumeSource}
\end{array}
\]
records a local carrier, local-ring label, residue prime, finite-extension
degree, integral structure, compact-open subset, uniformizer-scaled subset, and
their realization as regions in the current real-line copy.  It includes the
IUT~IV Proposition~1.4 normalization laws needed in the present corridor:
the integral structure has normalized log-volume zero, the normalized
log-volume is the degree-normalized raw log-volume, and multiplication by a
uniformizer shifts the normalized log-volume by \(-\log(p)\).  Lean constructs
\(\texttt{IUTStage1LocalCompactOpenTensorFactorSource}\) from this datum.
The finite direct-sum layer
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1NonarchimedeanLocalTensorRegionDirectSumSource}
\end{array}
\]
then constructs the compact-open tensor-region source from a finite family of
these local nonarchimedean sources and the direct-sum tensor-region formula.
Finally,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395NonarchimedeanLocalTensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
uses one such local tensor source for each charted localization cell, verifies
the local compact-open regions and local-ring labels against the charted factors,
constructs the compact-open tensor-packet source, and inherits the finite-additive
cover and bundle-log-volume conclusions.
The local nonarchimedean source has now been lowered once more to the
finite-extension Haar normalization boundary of IUT~IV, Proposition~1.4.  The
declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1FiniteExtensionHaarCompactOpenLogVolumeSource}
\end{array}
\]
records the raw Haar/log-volume function on local compact-open subsets of a
finite extension of \(\mathbb{Q}_p\), its degree-normalized version, the
realization of local subsets as real-line regions, the integral structure
\(\mathcal{O}_K\), and the uniformizer-scaled compact-open subset.  Its endpoint
checks the source-paper normalizations
\[
  \mu_{\log}(\mathcal{O}_K)=0,\qquad
  \mu_{\log}(p\cdot U)=\mu_{\log}(U)-\log(p),
\]
and constructs
\(\texttt{IUTStage1NonarchimedeanLocalCompactOpenLogVolumeSource}\).
The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1FiniteExtensionTensorProductDirectSumDecompositionSource}
\end{array}
\]
records the IUT~IV direct-sum decomposition step for finite tensor products over
\(\mathbb{Z}_p\): the tensor-product region is identified with the simultaneous
local compact-open cell, and its normalized log-volume is the finite sum of the
degree-normalized Haar log-volumes of the direct summands.  This source constructs
the nonarchimedean local tensor-region direct-sum source.  At the packet level,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395FiniteExtensionHaarTensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
assigns such a finite-extension Haar tensor decomposition to each charted
localization cell and then constructs the nonarchimedean local tensor-packet
source used by the Step~(xi) cover route.
The finite-extension Haar source has now been lowered to compact-open topology
provenance.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1FiniteExtensionCompactOpenTopologyHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
records the compact-open predicate on the local carrier, closure of
compact-opens under finite intersections, the ring-of-integers compact-open, the
chosen compact-open subset, a uniformizer action preserving compact-opens, the
raw Haar measure, and the raw and degree-normalized Haar log-volume functions.
Its endpoint verifies compact-open provenance for
\(\mathcal{O}_K\), \(U\), and \(p\cdot U\), checks
\(\log(\mu_{\mathrm{Haar}}(U))\) at the raw level, and constructs
\(\texttt{IUTStage1FiniteExtensionHaarCompactOpenLogVolumeSource}\).
The tensor layer
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1CompactOpenTopologyTensorProductDirectSumSource}
\end{array}
\]
constructs the finite-extension tensor-product direct-sum source from these
compact-open topology factors.  Finally,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395CompactOpenTopologyHaarTensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
feeds compact-open topology/Haar normalization data for each charted cell into
the finite-extension Haar tensor-packet source and hence into the same
finite-additive Step~(xi) cover route.
The local compact-open topology source has also been lowered one step further to
a Haar-measure-backed source.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1AdditiveHaarCompactOpenNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
uses mathlib's additive Haar-measure class on the local additive carrier,
records openness and compactness for the ring of integers and selected
compact-open subset, normalizes the ring of integers to Haar mass \(1\), and
records the finite-extension uniformizer scaling law for real Haar mass.  Lean
then derives the raw logarithmic shift by
\(-[K:\mathbb{Q}_p]\log(p)\), divides by the finite-extension degree, and
obtains the normalized IUT~IV shift \(\mu_{\log}(pU)=\mu_{\log}(U)-\log(p)\).
The companion declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1AdditiveHaarTensorProductDirectSumSource}
\end{array}
\]
feeds these Haar-backed local factors into the compact-open tensor/direct-sum
source, so the tensor summation layer now has a route whose local inputs are
actual additive Haar measures rather than arbitrary real-valued Haar functions.
There is now a valuation-ball refinement below this Haar source.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ProperUltrametricValuationBallTopologySource}
\end{array}
\]
now starts from a proper ultrametric metric topology on the local additive
carrier.  The ultrametric inequality proves openness of positive-radius closed
balls, while properness supplies compactness by the closed-ball compactness
theorem.  Thus the compact-open valuation-ball theorem is constructed from
two recognizable local topological hypotheses rather than from separate
open/compact fields.  The companion declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ProperUltrametricValuationBallAdditiveHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
feeds this proper-ultrametric source into the ultrametric Haar route.
The local ring input has also been sharpened from an abstract unit-ball label
to the valued-field integer subring supplied by \texttt{mathlib}.  The
declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ValuedFieldIntegerUnitBallSource}
\end{array}
\]
works over a nontrivially normed ultrametric field and uses
\texttt{Valued.integer.mem\_iff} to prove
\[
  \mathcal{O}_K=\{x\mid \|x\|\leq 1\}=\overline{B}(0,1).
\]
It then identifies this valued-field integer subring with the radius-one ball
in the proper-ultrametric valuation-ball topology.  The companion declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ValuedFieldIntegerProperUltrametric}\\
\quad\texttt{HaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
uses \(\mathcal{O}_K\) itself as the local-ring label and transports the Haar
mass-one normalization from \(\mathcal{O}_K\) to the radius-one valuation ball
before projecting into the proper-ultrametric Haar normalization route.
There is now a base local-field specialization of this statement.  The
declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1PadicIntegerUnitBallSource}
\end{array}
\]
works over \(\mathbb{Q}_p\), identifies
\(\mathcal{O}_{\mathbb{Q}_p}\) with \(\texttt{PadicInt.subring}\ p\), and
proves that its underlying set is the image of the coercion
\(\mathbb{Z}_p\hookrightarrow\mathbb{Q}_p\).  This also records the local-ring
instance on \(\mathbb{Z}_p\), so the ring-of-integers object is no longer only
the abstract valued-field subring.  The base residue quotient has now also
been made concrete.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1PadicIntegerResidueQuotientSource}
\end{array}
\]
uses the mathlib reduction map
\(\texttt{PadicInt.toZMod}:\mathbb Z_p\to \mathbb Z/p\mathbb Z\),
proves that its additive kernel is the maximal ideal of \(\mathbb Z_p\), and
applies the first isomorphism theorem to identify
\[
  \mathbb Z_p/\ker(\texttt{toZMod})\simeq_{\rm add}\mathbb Z/p\mathbb Z.
\]
Transporting the \(\mathbb Z/p\mathbb Z\)-vector-space structure across this
additive equivalence gives a one-dimensional residue module, and Lean proves
\[
  \#(\mathbb Z_p/\ker(\texttt{toZMod}))
    =p=p^{\operatorname{finrank}_{\mathbb Q_p}\mathbb Q_p}.
\]
The same source now also constructs
\[
  \texttt{Fin}(p^{[\mathbb Q_p:\mathbb Q_p]})
    \simeq \mathbb Z_p/\ker(\texttt{toZMod})
\]
and finite-index representatives whose quotient classes are definitionally
the indexed residue classes.  This upgrades the base-field residue quotient
from a cardinality result to the representative data needed by the coset
partition layer, without a supplied finite quotient equivalence.  This has now
been threaded into the base local coset/Haar boundary.  The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1PadicBaseFieldResidueQuotientDilationCoset}\\
\quad\texttt{HaarCharacterNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
constructs the additive equivalence
\[
  \mathbb Z_p \simeq_{\rm add} \mathcal O_{\mathbb Q_p},
\]
proves that the transported \(\ker(\texttt{toZMod})\) is exactly the subgroup
\(p\mathcal O_{\mathbb Q_p}\), applies the first isomorphism theorem to build
\[
  \mathcal O_{\mathbb Q_p}/p\mathcal O_{\mathbb Q_p}
    \simeq_{\rm add}
  \mathbb Z_p/\ker(\texttt{toZMod}),
\]
and then supplies the finite quotient equivalence and representatives consumed
by the quotient-coset partition/Haar-character source.  Thus the base-field
coset decomposition used to derive
\(\mu(p\mathcal O_{\mathbb Q_p})=p^{-1}\) now starts from the concrete
\(\texttt{PadicInt.toZMod}\) residue quotient rather than from a supplied
quotient package.  The companion
declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1PadicProperUltrametricHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
fixes the residue prime to \(p\), the finite-extension degree to \(1\), and the
uniformizer scale map to \(x\mapsto px\), then projects to the valued-field
integer Haar route.  The Haar mass-one and \(p\)-scaling law are still carried
as analytic local-field inputs, but their ambient field, local ring, residue
prime, degree, and uniformizer map are now the actual \(p\)-adic ones.  This
base local-field source now also projects into the finite-extension Haar
boundary itself by viewing \(\mathbb Q_p/\mathbb Q_p\) as a finite extension.
Lean constructs
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1PadicProperUltrametricHaarNormalizationSource.}\\
\quad\texttt{toPadicFiniteExtensionProperUltrametricHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
and proves that its valued-field integer projection agrees with the direct
\(\mathbb Q_p\) valued-field Haar source.  Thus the finite-extension degree
appearing in the normalization is not an independent parameter at the base
place: it is \(\operatorname{finrank}_{\mathbb Q_p}(\mathbb Q_p)=1\), with the
same base-prime dilation \(x\mapsto px\).
The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1UltrametricValuationBallTopologySource}
\end{array}
\]
starts from an ultrametric metric topology on the local additive carrier and
proves that every positive-radius closed valuation ball
\(\{x\mid d(x,0)\leq r\}\), \(r>0\), is open.  It still carries compactness of
these balls as the local compactness/properness input, but the openness part of
the compact-open assertion is now derived from the nonarchimedean triangle
inequality rather than supplied independently.  The companion declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1UltrametricValuationBallAdditiveHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
projects this ultrametric source into the positive-radius topology-backed Haar
route.
The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1PositiveRadiusValuationBallTopologySource}
\end{array}
\]
isolates the local-field topological theorem that every positive-radius
valuation ball \(\{x\mid \|x\|_v\leq r\}\), \(r>0\), is compact-open.  The
topology-backed declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ValuationBallTopologyAdditiveHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
then derives the unit ball and selected ball compact-open predicates from this
single positive-radius theorem before projecting to the older additive Haar
normalization route.  Thus the source boundary has moved from four separate
open/compact fields for two balls to one uniform valuation-ball compact-open
theorem.
The declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ValuationBallAdditiveHaarNormalizationSource}
\end{array}
\]
records a nonarchimedean valuation-norm function on the local carrier and defines
the ring of integers as the unit ball \(\{x\mid \|x\|_v\leq 1\}\).  The selected
local compact-open subset is likewise a valuation ball
\(\{x\mid \|x\|_v\leq r\}\) for a positive radius \(r\), and the uniformizer
operation is the image under a pointwise scale map.  Lean derives the compact-open
predicate as \(\texttt{IsOpen}\wedge\texttt{IsCompact}\), proves closure under
finite intersections in a \(T_2\) space, and constructs the additive Haar
normalization source from the valuation-ball data.  The companion tensor source
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ValuationBallTensorProductDirectSumSource}
\end{array}
\]
feeds valuation-ball local factors into the additive Haar tensor/direct-sum
source.
The valuation-ball route now also reaches the charted Step~(xi) cover boundary
itself.  The new declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395ValuationBallHaarTensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
assigns to each charted localization cell a valuation-ball tensor/direct-sum
source, proves that every local charted region and local-ring label is realized
by the corresponding valuation-ball factor, and then constructs the existing
compact-open topology/Haar tensor-packet cover source.  Its endpoint exposes
the valuation-ball identities for \(\mathcal{O}_K\) and \(U\), compact-openness
of the selected valuation balls, the finite direct-product cell log-volume
formula, the finite-additive cover sum, and the inherited bundle-log-volume
projection.  Thus the current IUT~IV local-volume corridor now proceeds from
valuation balls to additive Haar normalization, then to compact-open topology,
finite-extension Haar log-volume, tensor/direct-sum summation, and finally the
charted Step~(xi) cover route.
The local chart calibration in this valuation-ball route has now been pushed
down another level.  The per-factor declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1ValuationBallVectorBundleFactorCalibrationSource}
\end{array}
\]
constructs the local-ring chart from a valuation-ball Haar factor itself: the
chart local ring is the valuation-ball factor's local ring, and the chart region
is the realized selected valuation ball.  Its source law identifies the
localized vector-bundle direct summand with the normalized Haar log-volume of
that valuation ball, after which \Lean{} derives the ordinary chart/direct-summand
calibration source.  The packet-level declaration
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395ValuationBallFactorCalibratedHaarTensorPacket}\\
\quad\texttt{FiniteAdditiveCalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}
\end{array}
\]
uses these per-factor valuation-ball calibrations to build the previous
valuation-ball charted-cover source.  Thus the factor chart is no longer a
separate object merely matched to valuation-ball data; at this boundary it is
constructed from the valuation-ball compact-open region.  This same
factor-calibrated valuation-ball source now also projects into the newer
finite-cover-additive/tensor-measure-backed cover corridor.  The projection
uses the broad finite-additive law only to construct the selected
family-local finite-cover certificate, then \Lean{} derives the tensor-cell
cover sum
\[
  \mu_{\log}\Bigl(\bigcup_\beta H_\beta\Bigr)
    =
  \sum_\beta \mu_{\log}^{\mathrm{tensor}}(H_\beta)
\]
and reads the adjusted Ob3/Ob5 determinant equalities from that constructed
finite-cover source.  This connects the valuation-ball Haar factor route to the
current narrower cover-audit path without treating the tensor-cover theorem as
an independent payload.
The record-canonical valuation-ball handoff has also been tightened at the
source-core boundary.  The theorem
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395RecordOb3Ob5AdjustedDeterminantLogVolumeSource}\\
\quad\texttt{.ofValuationBallFactorCalibratedHaarTensorPacketFiniteAdditive}\\
\quad\texttt{CalibratedLocalRingChartedVectorBundleHullCoverSource}\\
\quad\texttt{\_toSourceCoreAdjustedLogVolumeSource\_eq}
\end{array}
\]
proves that, once the valuation-ball possible-image family is synchronized
with the Theorem~3.11 record family, the record-canonical Ob3/Ob5 source
forgets back to exactly the valuation-ball adjusted determinant log-volume
source.  Downstream principal valuation-ball finite-divisor sources can
therefore use this equality as a derived synchronization, rather than carrying
the valuation-ball Ob3/Ob5 equality as an unrelated payload.
This summand-calibrated source now feeds the milestone-facing constructed
Step~(xi) source directly.  The new constructor
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395RecordOb3Ob5AdjustedDeterminantLogVolumeSource}\\
\quad\texttt{.toConstructedHolomorphicHullDeterminantSource}
\end{array}
\]
first derives the record Ob3/Ob5 compatibility object from the finite summand
formula, then uses that derived compatibility to build
\(\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395ConstructedHolomorphicHullDeterminantSource}\).
The experiment endpoint
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{remark395RecordOb3Ob5AdjustedDeterminantLogVolumeSource}\\
\quad\texttt{\_toConstructedHolomorphicHullDeterminantSource\_endpoint}
\end{array}
\]
returns the finite-summand equality, the determinant and normalized determinant
identifications, and the chain
\[
  \mu_{\log}(q) \leq \det_{\log}(P_B) \leq \Theta_{\mathrm{signed}},
\]
so the constructed Step~(xi) route no longer receives the canonical
hull--determinant compatibility as an independent input in this constructor.
This constructed-source layer now also has an exact-theta refinement,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395RecordOb3Ob5AdjustedDeterminantLogVolumeSource}\\
\quad\texttt{.toConstructedHolomorphicHullDeterminantSource}\\
\quad\texttt{OfThetaEqFamilyHullLogVolume}.
\end{array}
\]
For an arbitrary q-region \(q\subseteq P_{\mathrm{rec}}\) contained in the
record possible-image union, this constructor derives the Ob4 normalized
tensor-power bound from
\[
  \theta_{\mathrm{signed}}
    =
  \mu_{\log}(\phi(P_B)),
\]
using the bounded-family hull/determinant source projected from the Ob3/Ob5
compatibility.  Its public endpoint records the exact-theta equality, the
derived tensor-power inequality, the adjusted-summand-to-determinant
identifications, the two-step hull/determinant chain, and
\(q_{\mathrm{signed}}\le\theta_{\mathrm{signed}}\).  Thus the general
constructed Step~(xi) source has the same no-free-tensor-bound interface that
was previously only available after choosing a possible-image q-region; the
package measure calibration and the record-canonical bridge equality remain
explicit source obligations.
There is now also an obligations-backed form of this arbitrary-q exact-theta
constructor,
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Remark395RecordOb3Ob5AdjustedDeterminantLogVolumeSource}\\
\quad\texttt{.toConstructedHolomorphicHullDeterminantSource}\\
\quad\texttt{OfThetaEqFamilyHullLogVolumeFromObligations}.
\end{array}
\]
It projects the package hull/determinant bridge equality, q-pilot positivity,
and source normalization from one
\(\texttt{IUTStage1SourceHullDetObligations}\) object.  The endpoint still
exposes the synchronization identifying that obligations-backed bridge datum
with the record-canonical Remark~3.9.5 hull/tensor-power construction for the
chosen q-region.  Thus, at the general constructed-source level, the remaining
explicit inputs are the measure calibration, the exact-theta family-hull

The endpoint type \texttt{Stage1Comparison} is not a source proof: its
comparison field is the Corollary-3.12-shaped conclusion, and the corresponding
theorem is only a projection.  The source-facing route must construct this
endpoint from the ledger.  The ledger now records the opaque output
certification and ties the \(\Theta\)-common bound used in the final inequality
to \texttt{chartedContainer.apply certificate}, so the displayed charted
container cannot be paired with an unrelated convenient bound.  Throughout the
current corridor, ``upper ray'' means the signed-log region
\(\{x\mid x\le b\}\), not the ordinary order-theoretic ray \(\{x\mid b\le x\}\).

The largest engineering issue has been reduced to the remaining organization of
the endpoint-route families.  Eight mechanical splits have been made:
\texttt{IUTStage1IUTIVAlgebra.lean} now
carries the Remark 3.12 sign shadows and the conditional \IUT{} IV
real-algebra handoff estimates, while \texttt{IUTStage1FiniteLabels.lean}
carries the finite-label and theta-root cusp-label source layer, and
\texttt{IUTStage1StepX.lean} carries the Step (x) upper-ray corridor together
with its boundary Frobenioid-shift diagnostics.  The Gaussian and
Hodge--Arakelov theta-evaluation shadow layer now lives in
\texttt{IUTStage1Gaussian.lean}, and the Hodge/SHE support layer now lives in
\texttt{IUTStage1HodgeSHE.lean}.  The Theorem 3.11 source-choice and
multiradial possible-image layer now lives in
\texttt{IUTStage1Theorem311.lean}.  The Step (xi) hull/determinant and \(\IPL\)
source layer now lives in \texttt{IUTStage1StepXI.lean}.  The first endpoint
audit family and nonarchimedean realified-Frobenioid/log-Kummer support layer
now live in \texttt{IUTStage1FrobenioidShift.lean}; the original
\texttt{IUTStage1Source.lean} file has now also been split into
\texttt{IUTStage1EndpointAudit.lean}, for the nested LogVolumeChartAudit
refinements, and \texttt{IUTStage1Source.lean}, for the public
source-package audit surface.  Low-risk future refactors are:
\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{Structured endpoint route families} & \text{smaller route modules},\\
\text{Generated dependency/audit report} & \text{separate checked target}.
\end{array}
\]
These refactors should be mechanical only: move declarations, preserve names
where possible, and rebuild after each move.

\section{Paper Trace Audit}

The current source map for the Theorem~3.11 to Corollary~3.12 corridor is now
recorded directly in Lean, rather than only in prose.  The namespace
\[
\begin{array}{l}
\texttt{IUTStage1Theorem311ToCorollary312PaperTrace}
\end{array}
\]
contains four obligation records and one assembled trace record.  The first
record covers IUT~III, Theorem~3.11 and Remarks~3.11.2--3.11.4: construction
of the multiradial representation, input-prime-strip link, theta-pilot possible
images, log-theta-lattice procession data, \(F_l\)-label transitions, and the
typed compatibility between possible images and the \((\Ind_1,\Ind_2)\)
equality quotient.  It explicitly keeps the \((\Ind_3)\) contribution as an
upper-semi log-volume inequality.
At the current strict endpoint these trace slots are witnessed by the quotient
equality, the typed-core action-law audit, the quotient-indexed pullback of
possible images, the exact \(|Z/lZ|=l\) cardinality, and the finite procession
transition law, rather than by a single broad quotient-audit wrapper.
The input-prime-strip and Hodge/\(\SHE/\IPL/\APT\) entries are likewise no
longer filled by the whole bridge audit at this strict boundary: the former is
the choice-wise constructed \(\IPL\) link endpoint, and the latter is the
structured \(\IPL/\SHE/\APT\) evidence together with the forbidden
\(\SHE\)-transport guard and the non-forbidden permitted \(\APT\) arrow.
The typed quotient layer now also has a first-class hull/log-volume
compatibility object,
\texttt{EqualityQuotientHullLogVolumeCompatibility}.  It packages the
quotient-indexed possible-image family with a Remark~3.9.5 hull operator,
proves pullback to the original choice-indexed images, proves equality-orbit
invariance for the resulting hull log-volumes under \((\Ind_1)\) and
\((\Ind_2)\), and keeps the \((\Ind_3)\) statement as the typed core's
upper-semi log-volume inequality rather than turning it into a hull equality.
The strict two-point nonvacuity model now instantiates this object as
\texttt{strictFiniteToyEqualityQuotientHullLogVolumeCompatibility}; its audit
endpoint verifies pullback, \((\Ind_1)\)/\((\Ind_2)\) hull-log-volume
invariance, the one-sided \((\Ind_3)\) core inequality, and the fact that the
strict \((\Ind_3)\) step is not collapsed by the equality quotient.  This is a
test of the interface geometry, not a claim that the finite model is a source
model of IUT.
